   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">

      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the europarty established in 1992. For the Socialists &amp; Democrats Group in the European Parliament, see 
       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats</a>.

      <p>The <b>Party of European Socialists</b> (<b>PES</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomson2011_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomson2011-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The PES comprises national-level political parties from all <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) plus Norway. This includes major parties such as the Italian <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">Democratic Party</a>, the British <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>, the French <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(France)" title="Socialist Party (France)">Socialist Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a>. Parties from a number of other European countries are also admitted to the PES as associate or observer parties.<sup id="cite_ref-MemberParties_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MemberParties-7">[7]</a></sup> Most member, associate and observer parties are members of the wider <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance" title="Progressive Alliance">Progressive Alliance</a> or <a href="/wiki/Socialist_International" title="Socialist International">Socialist International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ProgressiveAlliance_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProgressiveAlliance-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SocialistInternational_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SocialistInternational-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The PES is currently led by its president <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Stanishev" title="Sergei Stanishev">Sergei Stanishev</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bulgaria" title="Prime Minister of Bulgaria">Prime Minister of Bulgaria</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">political group in the European Parliament</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats</a> (S&amp;D). The PES also operates in the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_the_Regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee of the Regions">Committee of the Regions</a> (in the <a href="/wiki/PES_Group_in_the_Committee_of_the_Regions" class="mw-redirect" title="PES Group in the Committee of the Regions">PES Group in the Committee of the Regions</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>. </p>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#European_Commission"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">European Commission</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#European_Council"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">European Council</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#European_Council_and_Council_of_Ministers"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">European Council and Council of Ministers</span></a> 
           <ul> 
            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#Overview"><span class="tocnumber">4.5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Overview</span></a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe"><span class="tocnumber">4.6</span> <span class="toctext">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Committee_of_the_Regions"><span class="tocnumber">4.7</span> <span class="toctext">Committee of the Regions</span></a></li> 
         </ul> </li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li> 
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The party's English name is "Party of European Socialists". In addition, the following names are used in other languages: </p> 
      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 26em; -webkit-column-width: 26em; column-width: 26em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Partia e Socialistëve Europianë</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>: <i lang="bs">Partija evropskih socijalista/Партија европских социјалиста</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">Партия на европейските социалисти</span></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>: <i lang="hr">Stranka europskih socijalista</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Strana evropských socialistů</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <i lang="da">De Europæiske Socialdemokrater</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Partij van Europese Socialisten</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et">Euroopa Sotsialistlik Partei</i></li>

        <li><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Parti socialiste européen</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Sozialdemokratische Partei Europas</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Ευρωπαϊκό Σοσιαλιστικό Κόμμα</span></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">Európai Szocialisták Pártja</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>: <i lang="is">Flokkur evrópskra sósíalista</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">Páirtí na Sóisialaithe Eorpach</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Partito del Socialismo Europeo</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">Eiropas Sociāldemokrātiskā partija</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>: <i lang="lt">Europos socialistų partija</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourgish language">Luxembourgish</a>: <i lang="lb">Partei vun den Europäesche Sozialisten</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Партија на европските социјалисти</span></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>: <i lang="mt">Partit tas-Soċjalisti Ewropej</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a>: <i lang="no">Det europeiske sosialdemokratiske partiet</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Partia Europejskich Socjalistów</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Partido Socialista Europeu</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">Partidul Socialiștilor Europeni</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Партија европских социјалиста</span></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <i lang="sk">Strana európskych socialistov</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>: <i lang="sl">Stranka evropskih socialistov</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Partido de los Socialistas Europeos</i></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Europeiska socialdemokratiska partiet</i></li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <p>In March 2014 following the congress in Rome, the PES added the <a href="/wiki/Tagline" title="Tagline">tagline</a> "Socialists and Democrats" to its name following the admission of Italy's <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">Democratic Party</a> into the organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1961, the Socialists in the European Parliament attempted to produce a common 'European Socialist Programme' but this was neglected due to the applications of Britain, Denmark, Ireland and Norway to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a>. The Socialists' 1962 congress pushed for greater democratisation and powers for Parliament, though it was only in 1969 that this possibility was examined by the member states.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1973, Denmark, Ireland and the United Kingdom joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a>, bringing in new parties from these countries. The enlarged Socialist Congress met in <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a> and inaugurated the <i>Confederation of the Socialist Parties of the European Community</i>. The Congress also passed a resolution on <a href="/wiki/Social_policy" title="Social policy">social policy</a>, including the right to decent work, <a href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">social security</a>, democracy and <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">equality</a> in the European economy.<sup id="cite_ref-history_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1978, the Confederation of Socialist Parties approved the first common European election Manifesto. It focused on several goals among which the most important were to ensure a right to <a href="/wiki/Decent_work" title="Decent work">decent work</a>, fight pollution, end <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a>, protect the consumer and promote peace, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> and civil liberties. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>At its Luxembourg Congress in 1980, the Confederation of Socialist Parties approved its first Statute. The accession of Greece to the EU in 1981, followed by Spain and Portugal in 1986, brought in more parties. </p>
      <p>In 1984, a common Socialist election manifesto proposed a socialist remedy for the economic crisis of the time by establishing a link between industrial production, protection of fundamental social benefits, and the fight for an improved <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1992, with the European Community becoming the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Maastricht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Maastricht">Treaty of Maastricht</a> establishing the framework for political parties at a European level, the Confederation of Socialist Parties voted to transform itself into the Party of European Socialists. The party's first programme concentrated on job creation, democracy, <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, environmental and consumer protection, peace and security, regulation of immigration, discouragement of racism and fighting organised crime.<sup id="cite_ref-history_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Along with the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Socialist Group in the European Parliament</a>, the founding members of the PES were:<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Austria" title="Social Democratic Party of Austria">Social Democratic Party of Austria</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Parti_Socialiste_(Belgium)" title="Parti Socialiste (Belgium)">Socialist Party</a> (Francophone) and the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_Different" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Party Different">Socialist Party</a> (Flemish) of Belgium</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Social_Democrats_(Denmark)" title="Social Democrats (Denmark)">Social Democrats</a> of Denmark</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(France)" title="Socialist Party (France)">Socialist Party</a> of France</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a> of Greece</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a> of Ireland</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Italian_Democratic_Socialist_Party" title="Italian Democratic Socialist Party">Italian Democratic Socialist Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party" title="Italian Socialist Party">Italian Socialist Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_the_Left" title="Democratic Party of the Left">Democratic Party of the Left</a> of Italy</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Luxembourg Socialist Workers' Party">Luxembourg Socialist Workers' Party</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Labour Party (Netherlands)">Labour Party</a> of the Netherlands</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Portugal)" title="Socialist Party (Portugal)">Socialist Party of Portugal</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Swedish Social Democratic Party">Swedish Social Democratic Party</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a> of the UK</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2004 <a href="/wiki/Poul_Nyrup_Rasmussen" title="Poul Nyrup Rasmussen">Poul Nyrup Rasmussen</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Giuliano_Amato" title="Giuliano Amato">Giuliano Amato</a> to be elected President of the PES, succeeding <a href="/wiki/Robin_Cook" title="Robin Cook">Robin Cook</a> in the post. He was re-elected for a further 2.5 years at the PES Congress in Porto on 8 December 2006 and again at the Prague Congress in 2009. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2010, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Foundation_for_European_Progressive_Studies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Foundation for European Progressive Studies (page does not exist)">Foundation for European Progressive Studies</a> was founded as the <a href="/wiki/Political_foundation_at_European_level" title="Political foundation at European level">political foundation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a>) of the PES. </p>
      <p>Mr Rasmussen stood down at the PES Progressive Convention in Brussels on 24 November 2011. He was replaced as interim president by <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Stanishev" title="Sergei Stanishev">Sergei Stanishev</a>, chairman of the Bulgarian Socialist Party (BSP) and former prime minister of Bulgaria. </p>
      <p>On 28-29 September 2012, the PES Congress in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Congress elected interim president <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Stanishev" title="Sergei Stanishev">Sergei Stanishev</a> as full President, as well as four deputies: Jean-Christophe Cambadélis (1st Vice-President – <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(France)" title="Socialist Party (France)">PS</a>), <a href="/wiki/Elena_Valenciano" title="Elena Valenciano">Elena Valenciano</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">PSOE</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jan_Royall" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Royall">Jan Royall</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Katar%C3%ADna_Neve%C4%8Falov%C3%A1" title="Katarína Neveďalová">Katarína Neveďalová</a> (<a href="/wiki/Direction_%E2%80%93_Social_Democracy" title="Direction – Social Democracy">Smer-SD</a>). The same Congress elected Achim Post (<a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">SPD</a>) as its new secretary general, and adopted a process which it described as "democratic and transparent" for electing its next candidate for Commission President in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The PES had already agreed in 2011 to use a <a href="/wiki/PES_presidential_primaries,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="PES presidential primaries, 2014">PES presidential primary</a> for the election. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

         <td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em"> 
          <div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">
           <div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;border-top:1px solid #B60202;background:transparent;padding-left:0.3em;text-align:center;color:black;">
            Variants
           </div>
           <div class="NavContent plainlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;margin-top:0;padding:0 0.6em 0.6em;">
            <div class="hlist">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_parties">Member parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Member parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The PES has thirty-three full member parties from each of the twenty-eight EU member states and Norway. There are a further thirteen associate and twelve observer parties from other European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-number_of_parties_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-number_of_parties-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constituent_organisations">Constituent organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Constituent organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The youth organisation of the PES is the <a href="/wiki/Young_European_Socialists" title="Young European Socialists">Young European Socialists</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=PES_Women&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="PES Women (page does not exist)">PES Women</a> is the party's women's organisation, led by <a href="/wiki/Zita_Gurmai" title="Zita Gurmai">Zita Gurmai</a>. The LGBTI campaign organisation is <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Rose" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainbow Rose">Rainbow Rose</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-How_work?_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_work?-18">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_memberships">International memberships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: International memberships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>PES is an associated organisation of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_International" title="Socialist International">Socialist International</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance" title="Progressive Alliance">Progressive Alliance</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="President_and_Presidency">President and Presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: President and Presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The President (currently former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bulgaria" title="Prime Minister of Bulgaria">Prime Minister of Bulgaria</a> <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Stanishev" title="Sergei Stanishev">Sergei Stanishev</a>) represents the party on a daily basis and chairs the Presidency, which also consists of the Secretary General, President of the S&amp;D group in Parliament and one representative per full/associate member party and organisation. They may also be joined by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a> (if a PES member), a PES <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">European Commissioner</a> and a representative from associate parties and organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-How_work?_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_work?-18">[16]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The parties meet at the party <i>Congress</i> twice every five years to decide on political orientation, such as adopting <a href="/wiki/Manifesto" title="Manifesto">manifestos</a> ahead of <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">elections</a>. Every year that the Congress does not meet, the Council (a smaller version of the Congress) shapes PES policy. The Congress also elects the party's President, Vice Presidents and the <i>Presidency</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-How_work?_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_work?-18">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>Leader's Conference</i> brings together Prime Ministers and Party Leaders from PES parties three to four times a year to agree strategies and resolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-How_work?_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_work?-18">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_election_primaries">European election primaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: European election primaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In December 2009, the PES decided to put forward a candidate for Commission President at all subsequent elections.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> On 1 March 2014, the PES organised for the first time a European election Congress where a Common Manifesto <sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> was adopted and the Common Candidate designate for the post of Commission President, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a>, was elected by over a thousand participants in Rome, Italy. PES member parties across Europe joined forces to campaign for the European elections, and a mass grassroots movement sprang up in support of Martin Schulz, aiming to ‘knock the vote’ in support of his candidacy. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="PES_in_the_European_institutions">PES in the European institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: PES in the European institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_of_the_European_institutions">Overview of the European institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Overview of the European institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Organisation</th> 
         <th>Institution</th> 
         <th>Number of seats </th>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: European Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: 
       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Commission">European Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: European Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">European Commissioners</a> are meant to remain independent, however there has been an increasing degree of <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner#Politicisation" title="European Commissioner">politicisation within the Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> In the current European Commission, eight of the Commissioners belong to the PES family. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Council">European Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: European Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Of the 28 heads of state and government that are members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, seven are from the PES, and therefore regularly attend PES summits to prepare for European Council meetings. </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" cellpadding="2" cellspacing="0" border="1" width="100%" style="border-collapse:collapse; border:#555"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Member State </th> 
         <th>Representative </th> 
         <th>Title </th> 
         <th>Political party </th> 
         <th>Member of the Council since </th> 
         <th class="unsortable" style="width:50px;">Photo </th>

      <p>Although the prime minister of Romania, <a href="/wiki/Mihai_Tudose" title="Mihai Tudose">Mihai Tudose</a>, is also a member of the PES (and his <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_(Romania)" title="Social Democratic Party (Romania)">Social Democratic Party</a> is a PES member party), Romania instead sends its <a href="/wiki/President_of_Romania" title="President of Romania">president</a> to the European Council. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Council_and_Council_of_Ministers">European Council and Council of Ministers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: European Council and Council of Ministers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_(18_December_2017).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_%2818_December_2017%29.png/300px-Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_%2818_December_2017%29.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_%2818_December_2017%29.png/450px-Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_%2818_December_2017%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_%2818_December_2017%29.png/600px-Party_affiliations_in_the_European_Council_%2818_December_2017%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1359" data-file-height="1244"></a>

      <p><a href="/wiki/Parties_in_the_European_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Parties in the European Council">Party-alignment at the European Council</a> is often loose, but has been the basis of some intergovernmental cooperation. At present seven countries are led by a PES-affiliated leader, who represents that state at the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>: Spain (<a href="/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez_(Spanish_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro Sánchez (Spanish politician)">Pedro Sánchez</a>), Portugal (<a href="/wiki/Antonio_Costa" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonio Costa">Antonio Costa</a>), Malta (<a href="/wiki/Joseph_Muscat" title="Joseph Muscat">Joseph Muscat</a>), Slovakia (<a href="/wiki/Peter_Pellegrini" title="Peter Pellegrini">Peter Pellegrini</a>), Denmark (<a href="/wiki/Mette_Frederiksen" title="Mette Frederiksen">Mette Frederiksen</a>), Finland (<a href="/wiki/Antti_Rinne" title="Antti Rinne">Antti Rinne</a>) and Sweden (<a href="/wiki/Stefan_L%C3%B6fven" title="Stefan Löfven">Stefan Löfven</a>). </p>
      <p>The makeup of national delegations to the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of Ministers</a> is at some times subject to coalitions: for the above governments led by a PES party, that party may not be present in all Council configurations; in other governments led by non-PES parties a PES minister may be its representative for certain portfolios. PES is in coalition in a further seven countries: Estonia, France, Germany, Luxembourg, Romania, Slovenia and Italy. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

       <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Group">Socialist Group</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Committee_of_the_Regions">Committee of the Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_European_Socialists&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Committee of the Regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>PES has 122 members in the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_the_Regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee of the Regions">Committee of the Regions</a> as of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-PES_Group_members_list_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PES_Group_members_list-23">[21]</a></sup> </p>

      <table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
